  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a011afa8-1594-4068-9654-ee12c67462cb'

<span id="freeTextContainer18302929897863227600"><i>When kingdom come, there will be one.</i><br/><br/>In every generation on the island of Fennbirn, a set of triplets is born—three queens, all equal heirs to the crown and each possessor of a coveted magic.   <span id="freeText18302929897863227600" style="display:none"><i>When kingdom come, there will be one.</i><br /><br />In every generation on the island of Fennbirn, a set of triplets is born—three queens, all equal heirs to the crown and each possessor of a coveted magic. Mirabella is a fierce elemental, able to spark hungry flames or vicious storms at the snap of her fingers. Katharine is a poisoner, one who can ingest the deadliest poisons without so much as a stomachache. Arsinoe, a naturalist, is said to have the ability to bloom the reddest rose and control the fiercest of lions.<br /><br />But becoming the Queen Crowned isn’t solely a matter of royal birth. Each sister has to fight for it. And it’s not just a game of win or lose…it’s life or death. The night the sisters turn sixteen, the battle begins.<br /><br />The last queen standing gets the crown. </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1272772095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2281617844350036001"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23207027.Three_Dark_Crowns__Untitled___1_' title='Three Dark Crowns (Untitled, #1) by Kendare Blake' rel='nofollow noopener'>Three Dark Crowns</a> has an interesting premise, but it manages to be insufferably boring for the first 75%. <b>I foresee many DNFs on the horizon for this book</b>.<br/><br/>It's about three sisters, three queens, essentially competing for the throne. They - Katharine, Arsinoe and Mirabella - each live in different parts of the land, each have a different power, and each have a different group of supporters aiding them. This is an "in every generation, there are three chosen ones..." kind of thing. However, throug</span>
  <span id="freeText2281617844350036001" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23207027.Three_Dark_Crowns__Untitled___1_" title="Three Dark Crowns (Untitled, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">Three Dark Crowns</a> has an interesting premise, but it manages to be insufferably boring for the first 75%. <b>I foresee many DNFs on the horizon for this book</b>.<br /><br />It's about three sisters, three queens, essentially competing for the throne. They - Katharine, Arsinoe and Mirabella - each live in different parts of the land, each have a different power, and each have a different group of supporters aiding them. This is an "in every generation, there are three chosen ones..." kind of thing. However, throughout the generations, only one sister can claim the throne, and she must do so by murdering the other two.<br /><br />In this case, Katharine is a poisoner who wields deadly cocktails; Arsinoe is a naturalist - at one with nature and animals - and not very good at it (nobody expects her to win the throne); Mirabella is an elemental and clearly the strongest of the three, her powers by far the most developed.<br /><br />It sounds quite exciting, but it is far <b>too slow and quiet a telling for such a nasty premise</b>. The first three quarters are just boring. They needed a shot of excitement. Most of the book consists of the girls honing their skills in their own private locations and having flirtations with their love interests. It is painfully hard to not yawn, put the book down, and go find something more riveting to do. Like watching paint dry, for example.<br /><br />I am not exaggerating. So little happens - there is no action, no drama, no excitement until near the end. And, by that point, how much do we really care? I don't know about you, but if I've spent most of a book being bored out of my mind, I'm not going to suddenly become invested when the pacing picks up.<br /><br />The book flits between third-person perspectives and, truly, none of them are interesting. Arsinoe mostly wanders around being useless and watching the romance between Jules and Joseph. Mirabella repeatedly plays with the elements, conjuring earthquakes and towers of fire. Katharine is perhaps most interesting, but mainly because she's dealing with scars and blisters from the latest poison she's ingested. That should tell you something about the bar for excitement in this book - the highlights are when one of the characters is sick from poisoning. Problem is, the three queens don't really get their hands dirty for the most part. <b>Their stories are not bloody and political, they are quiet and sometimes romantic.</b><br /><br />Yes, the pacing picks up towards the end. No, it wasn't enough for me. It might work better for extremely patient readers who can stomach a mostly non-existent plot. There are rare occasions where characters and writing can make up for very little happening, but for me, this is not one of them.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2281617844350036001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1251111006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251111006" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251111006?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23207027-three-dark-crowns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=cheesy-cheesy-cheesy">cheesy-cheesy-cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=derp-moments">derp-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=hate-the-characters-hate-the-book">hate-the-characters-hate-the-book</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-concept-poor-execution">great-concept-poor-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=i-spy-something-pointy">i-spy-something-pointy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251111006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13834029248566853691"><b>2.5 stars </b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"Three dark sisters<br/>All fair to be seen,<br/>Two to devour<br/>And one to be queen"</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348252ra/702518.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Three Dark Crowns <b>offends me.</b> It promised me scheming sisters and political intrigue and power plays. Instead I get this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476458062i/20844899.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476458062ra/20844900.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And a whole lot of this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476458062ra/20844901.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>80% of the book</b> is the sisters (Katharine, Mirabella, and Arinsoe) waffling around, training, and getting acquainted with their love interests. What's each island's culture? How did the tradition of Triplets Hunger Games begin? No fucking idea, but look, dream</span>
  <span id="freeText13834029248566853691" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars </b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Three dark sisters<br>All fair to be seen,<br>Two to devour<br>And one to be queen"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348252ra/702518.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Three Dark Crowns <b>offends me.</b> It promised me scheming sisters and political intrigue and power plays. Instead I get this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1476458062i/20844899.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476458062ra/20844900.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And a whole lot of this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476458062ra/20844901.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>80% of the book</b> is the sisters (Katharine, Mirabella, and Arinsoe) waffling around, training, and getting acquainted with their love interests. What's each island's culture? How did the tradition of Triplets Hunger Games begin? No fucking idea, but look, dreamy eyes!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476458062ra/20844902.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The romance itself isn't good either. Each sister has her own POV and love interest, but because of the multiple-POVs, <b>none of them are fleshed out.</b> Other than the sisters, side characters like Jules and Natalia have point-of-view chapters, too. It's a curious mixture of too much going on yet nothing happens. While I'm glad each sister queen has the chance to tell her side of the story, the feeling is dampened when it becomes a detriment rather than an advantage.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Joseph flings himself in front of a bear to protect Mirabella after knowing her for two days. TWO. DAYS.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/612019.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He is also an asshat of the highest order. He makes out with Mirabella, freaks out because he's cheating on Jules, then continues kissing her. What the actual fuck. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Perhaps it's the way Three Dark Crowns is written, but I <b>couldn't relate to any of the sisters.</b> It's third-person narrative at its worst, flat and emotionless. Plus, the sisters are individually insufferable. Katharine is a cowering sack of flour. Mirabella is a starry-eyed idealist with poor planning skills. Arinsoe reads like she's twelve and stamps her foot, pretending to be a strong female, but makes mistake after mistake.<br><br><b>Some of their plotlines make no sense.</b> Take Katharine's for instance. She receives seduction lessons from Pietyr, nephew of her mentor Natalia, to ensure her sisters do not get suitors. <b>What's the point?</b> So Mirabella and Arinsoe don't get suitors at the Quickening, a festival after which they can begin killing each other. They're humiliated and will probably act more ruthlessly against Katharine during in the coming year. Getting a king-consort isn't essential to winning the crown. It's just a way to set up her romance. I would rather see her sabotaging her sisters to make up for her weak gift, or work through the Black Council to push through a law that determines only a poisoner can be crowned. <br><br>There's a brilliant opportunity for female friendship, which is <b>absolutely squandered.</b> Jules, through which we first see Arinsoe, could have been a real breakout character. Yet she seems more interested in her boyfriend Joseph than her BFF's impending death. One of the reasons Three Dark Crowns' premise appealed to me is that it could morph into a beautiful story of girl power and sisterhood. Sadly, Jules's storyline is reflective of the actual product.<br><br>On whole, <b>Three Dark Crowns feels like a prequel.</b> The last 20% is amazing and should have been put in the front after a few lead-in chapters, the romances woven along the excitement and danger of the Ascension Year. As it currently stands, we have to wait until the next book to see the queens fight it out.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"They'll all pay for this," she said against his shoulder. "They will bleed and scream and get what they're owed."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476458062ra/20844903.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>More of this, please? Don't let me down again.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777270711" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of One Dark Throne</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2305869862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305869862" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305869862?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305869862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15410719921276642083">3.5 stars! I struggled with this start to a new series, but I’m currently reading the sequel and am SERIOUSLY enjoying it, so it was worthwhile for me to push through the first novel!<br/> <br/>I will always admit when I feel choosing the audio version of a book may have impacted my reading experience. I restarted the first few hours of <i>Three Dark Crowns</i> about four times because I just could not keep track of the story. And that was my biggest issue with this story – I just could not get engaged. There’s </span>
  <span id="freeText15410719921276642083" style="display:none">3.5 stars! I struggled with this start to a new series, but I’m currently reading the sequel and am SERIOUSLY enjoying it, so it was worthwhile for me to push through the first novel!<br /> <br />I will always admit when I feel choosing the audio version of a book may have impacted my reading experience. I restarted the first few hours of <i>Three Dark Crowns</i> about four times because I just could not keep track of the story. And that was my biggest issue with this story – I just could not get engaged. There’s a HUGE cast, a wide variety of perspectives, and many different locations and I struggled to keep everything at the forefront of the story while listening, but that’s not automatically a bad thing. I feel it is more a personal thing/my reading experience which caused me to have an extremely difficult time staying present in the story and remembering all the details and it’s possible the audio version had an impact on that.<br /> <br />I am also afraid my expectations may have influenced my reading experience as well. I believed <i>Three Dark Crowns</i> was going to be an epic battle between sisters for the crown, but I’ve found that’s more the focus of the sequel, <i>One Dark Throne</i>. <i>Three Dark Crowns</i> is VERY character based and the majority of the novel is more focused on getting to know the characters, understanding the magic system and monarchy, and “setting up” the events to take place in the ascension year. I think had I known this beforehand, I would have enjoyed it more so I could appreciate the detail put into character development and political ties without waiting for a greater amount of action scenes, because those are all things I really enjoy in fantasy novels! If you like a more character-driven fantasy story with political intrigue, I feel <i>Three Dark Crowns</i> would be of interest to you. If you’re looking for the story of sisters competing to the death, I believe you’ll need to keep reading for book two.<br /> <br />I feel the world and characters were really well-developed. There’s so much care put into developing the history of the Island, the workings of the monarchy’s rituals/traditions, and tensions between different sects of the island and the queens that represent them. The magic system really impressed me. It is much grander and more expansive than I initially anticipated, and I cannot wait to see it develop in future books. The side characters did not grasp me all that much but Katherine, Mirabella, Arsinoe and Jules were all very unique and I enjoyed reading from their perspective. I adored each of their individual character arcs and how they develop through the story. Despite my troubles staying engaged with the story, there is so much to love about it.<br /> <br />I also want to add that although I felt the beginning was very slow paced and there weren’t that many significant, intense scenes occurring, the story really picked up by the end. The climax of the story/final cliffhanger really grasped me and I’m so happy I continue with this novel to the end. By the conclusion of the novel, I ended up totally falling in love with this series and consider it a worthwhile read as a whole.<br /> <br />Overall, <i>Three Dark Crowns</i> wasn’t my favorite reading experience in the history of literature, but I really enjoyed the story and am already continuing on with the series. <i>One Dark Throne</i> has already stepped up the game and I am so much more enthralled with the story. I really can’t wait to continue with this series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15410719921276642083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2035818554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2035818554" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2035818554?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2035818554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13780414158637645">UTTER DISAPPOINTMENT AT ITS FINEST. <br/><br/>Wow. Wow. Let me start off by saying that this is going to be messy and probably inarticulate. But just go with it. Had to let it out. <br/><br/>Alright. How does one express rage in just a few words? Because in the last quarter of this book (fine, all) - I had to constantly take breaks to calm and compose myself because I was too LIVID and could feel my blood boiling and chest pain arising. Then why, you may ask did I continue? <br/>Because 1) I hate DNFing books. 2) I hone</span>
  <span id="freeText13780414158637645" style="display:none">UTTER DISAPPOINTMENT AT ITS FINEST. <br /><br />Wow. Wow. Let me start off by saying that this is going to be messy and probably inarticulate. But just go with it. Had to let it out. <br /><br />Alright. How does one express rage in just a few words? Because in the last quarter of this book (fine, all) - I had to constantly take breaks to calm and compose myself because I was too LIVID and could feel my blood boiling and chest pain arising. Then why, you may ask did I continue? <br />Because 1) I hate DNFing books. 2) I honestly kept hoping that things would change by the end and that maybe, just maybe, my perspective would also change along with it. Neither did. <br />The book had an interesting premise that was executed so, so poorly. Horribly. <br /><br />First and foremost, can we talk about how mind-numbingly BORING it was?? How could a book fail to pick up three quarters in!? <br />Ahhh, and the gift that kept on giving. The horrible, atrocious and petulant cast of characters who ruined everything. EVERYTHING. 🤦‍♀️💆 <br /><br />1 - I fucking HATED HATED Joseph with a livid passion (why is it that we NEVER see accountability in YA Fantasy??) He was an irredeemable shithead through and through. <br /><br />2 - I grew to HATEEE Mirabella or whatever her name is. Her actions were absolutely disgusting. And the fact that she didn’t care was like throwing gasoline on a fire. <br /><br />3 - But what Really took the cake was the manner in which some (most, let’s face it) of the women were depicted. THIS. This is what got to me. <br />Why were they painted in such a horrible and weak light! They were contemptible, lacking in every sense of the word and downright loathsome! They were weak-willed and spineless who couldn’t think for themselves. <br /><br />- One couldn’t hold her ground when she should have (apologising and putting the blame on herself when she was the one wronged) what kind of example is that to young readers? Yes, a boy can treat you like shit but DO MAKE SURE that you’re the one who apologises.☝️<br /><br />- One was just a doormat. Who’d say ‘how high’ if/when told to jump. Yes. Since you’re a girl and (obviously) brainless, and he’s “hot” who treats you like his doll (really. He does) DO MAKE SURE that you submit to him and his every need. No questions asked. ☝️<br /><br />- One (oh this one 🤦‍♀️) - Fucking shameful. It is one thing to do something unknowingly. But repeating it with no thought to how it’d impact others even after being aware!? Because you’re that dumb? Oh, the list goes on with this bitch.<br /><br />- And of course. The men. Oh, how I HATED THEM. They were either misogynistic, dominating and arrogant shitheads or mind-numbingly boring.<br />And I know I’ve said it above but this bears repeating. I have never felt such hate of this magnitude for a male character like I have for Joseph. I LOATHED HIM WITH EVERYTHING IN ME. He was a worthless punchable trash. Simple as that. <br /><br />I fail to see what the point of this book was. What is the lesson here? Other than reading about horny brainless teenagers cheating left and right and dumb-as-hell girls being controlled by men because they weren’t given (by the author) the mental capacity to stand up for themselves. I mean, what does the reader get out of this horrid experience? <br /><br />A lot of the events that took place completely ruined the reading experience for me. And no, I don’t understand how these events could’ve been used as a way to drive this shit of a plot when all it did was make the cast seem like utter trash. <br /><br />It’s heartbreaking because I remember my excitement when I bought the book. I mean, I blew off a great book to read the atrocity that is this... ehmm book. <br /><br />These are horrible, terrible characters. Bad. Just bad! Yikes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13780414158637645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1642344215" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1642344215" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1642344215?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23207027-three-dark-crowns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642344215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer447516691105568348"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No one really wishes to be a queen.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Oh my, I loved this. This book seems to be very polarizing on my feed, and from people I love, trust, and have similar reading tastes as, so I was a little apprehensive going in. I read that first chapter with my mouth open the entire time. Instantly drawn in, immersed, and in love. <br/><br/>Most of you probably know the synopsis of this book, but it will still bring me immense joy to tell those few who might not know. Basically, this story is set in a wor</span>
  <span id="freeText447516691105568348" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No one really wishes to be a queen.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Oh my, I loved this. This book seems to be very polarizing on my feed, and from people I love, trust, and have similar reading tastes as, so I was a little apprehensive going in. I read that first chapter with my mouth open the entire time. Instantly drawn in, immersed, and in love. <br><br>Most of you probably know the synopsis of this book, but it will still bring me immense joy to tell those few who might not know. Basically, this story is set in a world with an amazing matriarchy, where a queen will always give birth to multiple girls. For the most part, it will be triplets, each with different powers, who will be sent away to live among people who have also developed their powers. Yet, once these sisters turn sixteen, a battle will begin which only ends when only one of the girls are alive and the other two sisters dead. This lone triplet will be the new queen of Fennbirn. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518571010i/25055804._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This world is gloriously feminist, and I loved each point of view from the different islands. And the writing? Beautiful, lyrical, genius. And I fell so very in love with each sister, easily, and happily. These characters are honestly a tier above almost every YA character I’ve ever read. And again, this was such an amazing journey and I hope more people give this book a shot, despite the mixed reviews. <br><br>And the twists and turns? I was at the edge of my seat reading this! And I was going to say one of the only downsides while reading was because a friend sort of intentionally spoiled a twist for me, but then I was completely blindsided by another immediately after. The only reason I chose to give this four stars, instead of five, was because the actual plot itself was a little slow for my liking. This is a very character driven story, and I loved that so much, but some major plot points just felt like they took too long to get going. Even though, once they did? Lord, help me. Perfection. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“In her mind, every last Queen lies at the bottom of the sea, drowned by the Goddess the moment she was done with them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>So, something I also really want to talk about is how this (in my mind and my opinion) is an own voices book. I watch a lot of Booktube, I read a lot of blogs, I spend too much time on book twitter, but I have never heard that Kendare Blake is Korean, ever. I noticed how the triplets’ descriptions were somewhat vague besides the dark black hair, so I went and did some searching, and I was absolutely shocked to find out that this book is written by a woman of color. I immediately went to snapchat, and all of my friends, too, did not know this. So, I just wanted to make this a point in my review, because me and so many of my friends want to support marginalized voices, and if I would have known this sooner, I wouldn’t have waited to pick this book up. On top of the fact that I loved it, and it was amazing, it warms my damn heart to picture three kickass Asian girls, trying to overcome to pressures that this world has put on them, while trying to decide their own destinies. Seriously, this meant so much to me. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1518571010i/25055803._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Breathing fanart by <a href="http://thesenesx.tumblr.com/post/165827449461/katharine-arsinoe-and-mirabella-from-three-dark" rel="nofollow noopener">TheSenesX</a><br><br>Okay, I’m going to do a quick breakdown of the three sisters! I found these amazing pictures from Epic Reads on my wonderful friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1793197104?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">May’s review</a> and I couldn’t resist adding them to mine, because they are so dang adorable and perfect! <br><br>➽<b>Katharine</b> 💚☠ - Gravesdrake Manor - Poisoner Queen<br>The poisoner queen always wins, so Katharine has a tremendous amount of pressure on her. But her body is weak and frail, from being forced to ingest so many poisons, and from the abuse she receives for not achieving her full potential. She is lonely, and scared, and somehow completely made her way into my heart. Katharine is my favorite of the three sisters. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480920389i/21363325._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽<b>Mirabella</b> 💙🔥 - Rolanth – Elementalist Queen<br>The strongest of the sisters. The world already tells tales of her power. She is almost guaranteed to be the next queen, but she is constantly struggling with the idea of killing her sisters. She was raised among the people of the temple on her small, but very religious, island. She, too, has felt really lonely growing up. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480920389i/21363327._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽<b>Arsinoe</b> ❤🐻 - Wolf Spring – Naturalist Queen<br>This sister for sure had the happiest upbringing, with friends and found family that actually loves her unconditionally. Sadly, she hasn’t developed any of her naturalist powers, but her best friend, Jules, is one of the strongest to have ever lived. She is desperate to develop any magical affinity, and starts tampering with magic that she probably shouldn’t, because this magic always comes with a price. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480920389i/21363326._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And even though Katharine is my favorite, I loved all three so much. And all three sisters are so beautifully morally grey, especially by the end of this story. Morally grey characters will forever by my favorites, and Kendare Blake gave me three strong, powerful, and smart ones to cry over and to root for. <br><br>Oh, and also, I told myself I wouldn’t devote a paragraph to this, but here we are with unpopular opinions: I don’t hate Joseph, not in the slightest. Like, did he do something he maybe shouldn’t have? Yes. Is this a realistic depiction of being a sixteen-year-old whose hormones are working double time? Yes. And I think he proved numerous times that he isn’t a bad guy. He does the “right” thing over and over, even if he is suppressing his own happiness. Also, I’m always here for all the sex positive depictions. More unpopular opinion: I totally ship him with the unpopular one to ship him with. Muahahahaha! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I should think that is what anyone would wish- to be loved for themselves and not their position.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, I truly loved this. I can see it being one of my all time favorite series. And I cannot wait to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2294965477" rel="nofollow noopener">One Dark Throne</a> immediately. Also, say a prayer for me that my Target still has the signed edition that I saw a few weeks ago. <br><br><b>Trigger/Content warnings:</b> abuse, violence, and animal death. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/jtotheimin" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://ko-fi.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Ko-fi</a> | <a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/meltotheany?si=kHJ5JnLHQsSp23fDe0qxSQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/33446050-kayla-b" rel="nofollow noopener">Kayla</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="447516691105568348" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1726901261" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1726901261" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1726901261?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=best-audiobooks">best-audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1726901261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4637361073978030821">4.5 stars. Wow this was bloody fantastic. <br/><br/>BUT.<br/><br/>The first 35% or so was ROUGH. I honestly would have DNF'ed this had it not been for friends telling me to keep going. I'M SO GLAD I DID. So if you're reading this and you get bored/overwhelmed with all the names/generally disinterested... it WILL pick up! (And don't worry about memorizing all the character names/who is who.)<br/><br/>Basically we have three triplets. They are separated at a young age and each raised in separate parts of the kingdom/island thi</span>
  <span id="freeText4637361073978030821" style="display:none">4.5 stars. Wow this was bloody fantastic. <br /><br />BUT.<br /><br />The first 35% or so was ROUGH. I honestly would have DNF'ed this had it not been for friends telling me to keep going. I'M SO GLAD I DID. So if you're reading this and you get bored/overwhelmed with all the names/generally disinterested... it WILL pick up! (And don't worry about memorizing all the character names/who is who.)<br /><br />Basically we have three triplets. They are separated at a young age and each raised in separate parts of the kingdom/island thing. Each of them is tailored to have one type of magic. When they reach 16, they are all supposed to face each other off with said magic, and whoever wins gets the throne. (Not only are they supposed to try and kill each other, they try to gain supporters and win suitors to help them in this.) Then, the surviving queen will choose a suitor who will act as 'king consort'. She will have said triplets (thanks to the curse on the island?), be sent away, rinse and repeat. Pretty depressing world, if you ask me. The general vibe is pretty dark and bleak, so be prepared.<br /><br />*Very Minor spoilers below*<br /><br />Anyway, I went into this fully expecting to favor one queen and not like the others- but I was surprised. I actually adored each of them - and felt really sorry for them. What I didn't expect was to get really invested in each of their stories AND all the suitors as well. Each queen has a "guy" that they are close to/favor... but things do not play out the way you'll expect them to. Shit gets cray. <br /><br />We have <b>Katherine</b> - who is the 'poisoner queen' raised by the Poisoners. Except, she's so incredibly weak and isn't actually showing strength digesting said poisons. She's forced to eat poisoned food all the time and is constantly sick. Since she appears so weak, her clan is greatly concerned and tries to fake her strength. Poor Kat pretty much knows she's going to die- so her only chance at survive is to learn how to "woo" all the suitors. Enter Peityr - the boy who offers to train her on how to woo men.<br /><br />Then there's <b>Arsinoe</b> who I just adored. She's strong, kind, and generally just badass. She's raised by the Naturalists who have a gift for animals. Each naturalist has the power to tame one animal - and that animal becomes theirs / they can control said animal for the rest of their life. Except Arsinoe can't seem to do that. But, she has dear friends and has a great attitude anyway -- though they don't expect her to live past the ascension year either. Then she meets Billy, and ... I can't say anything else.<br /><br /><b>Mirabella</b> is the strongest of all the queens - her gift as an elementalist (she can control elements/weather) is extremely powerful. Everyone expects her to easily win/outlive her sisters... BUT... she is so incredibly kind and doesn't want to hurt them. I CANT EVEN with the guy. I can't. I can't. I'm not saying that's a good or bad thing either. Just wait.<br /><br />AND THEN there's <b>Jules</b>, Arsinoe's best friend and very powerful naturalist who almost feels like a fourth main character. She has several POVs and she gets very tangled in things and her love story.. I can't. <br /><br />SOOOOOO all that to say... the story picks up and lightly introduces you to each queen and blah blah. But their stories get intermingled REALLY quickly. And it happens in ways you won't ever suspect. And it gets emotional. And I was flailing and freaking out and.... Ugh. Just read it.<br /><br />AND THEN THE END OHMERGSKERJSLKFJSLKDFJSLDKFJ. I DID NOT SEE THAT COMING. Okay okay, but everyone told me the end was crazy awesome- but just to give a heads up... it's not this huge action packed scene. It's one kicker at the very end. <br /><br />LSKDFJ:LSKDFJ HOW ARE WE SUPPOSED TO WAIT A YEAR FOR THE NEXT BOOK?!??!?! WHAT THE CRAP. <br /><br />Oh also, the audiobook was fantastic. LOVED the narrator. The writing felt a bit dry at the beginning and when I switched to audio, it felt a bit more lively! <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4637361073978030821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1350013699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1350013699" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1350013699?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23207027-three-dark-crowns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1350013699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4544849629507547507"><blockquote>
  <i>Three dark queens<br/>are born in a glen,<br/>sweet little triplets<br/>will never be friends.<br/><br/>Three dark sisters<br/>all fair to be seen,<br/>two to devour<br/>and one to be Queen.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This was SO much darker than I originally expected and it is GOOD. The world-building, the twists, the characters, the premise itself. It's hard not to be pulled deep into the story. Consider me invested! For a first book where clearly the concept had to be set up, as well as the world..I still found there was a lot going on. This just gives me</span>
  <span id="freeText4544849629507547507" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Three dark queens<br />are born in a glen,<br />sweet little triplets<br />will never be friends.<br /><br />Three dark sisters<br />all fair to be seen,<br />two to devour<br />and one to be Queen.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This was SO much darker than I originally expected and it is GOOD. The world-building, the twists, the characters, the premise itself. It's hard not to be pulled deep into the story. Consider me invested! For a first book where clearly the concept had to be set up, as well as the world..I still found there was a lot going on. This just gives me more hope for the second where I have a feeling there will be a lot more action and excitement.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23207027.Three_Dark_Crowns__Untitled___1_" title="Three Dark Crowns (Untitled, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener"> Three Dark Crowns</a> follows a set of triplets, all three queens - heirs to the crown, though only one will reign. All three born with a different gift. At the age of six, they are separated to be raised by different families each of their same respective gift giving each a completely different upbringing. The sisters don’t see each other again until they turn sixteen, when they will have to kill each other leaving only one to be the ruling queen of Fennbirn. Every generation a new set of triplets is born. This is how it has always been.<br /><br />Katharine is a poisoner. She’s supposed to be able to consume excruciating amounts of poison without any side-effects. The problem is Katharine’s gift is quite weak. The Arrons have been poisoning her as often as possible to try and build up her immunities. The result is a frail, feeble queen covered in scabs and other markings the poisoning attempts leave. The Arrons are desperate to keep a poisoner on the throne as it keeps their family on the Black Council. It has been a poisoner queen the last two years..<br /><br />Mirabella is an elemental giving her power over the elements such as fire, water, and wind. This includes some capability of creating nasty storms and it’s pretty badass. She has the strongest gift out of her sisters making her the clear contender for the crown. This is why the temple openly backs her (something unheard of in years past). They want power on the island and need a queen on their side to seize that power from the Black Council giving importance back to the temple. Is Mirabella the Queen they all believe her to be or is her heart having different ideas?<br /><br />Arsinoe is a naturalist. She should be able to make flowers bloom, have control over animals, and have an animal familiar. She cannot do any of these things and is still waiting on her gift. Her best friend Jules has an extremely strong naturalist gift giving her a mountain cat as a familiar. Arsinoe tried to escape her fate years ago by running away, but the island wouldn’t let her go leading to the banishment of Jules’ boy. One of the best things about Arsinoe is her loyalty to her friends. I love that the power of friendship truly means something to her.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Of course I do not wish that. No one really wishes to be a queen.</i>
</blockquote><br />To be a queen is to be cursed. Two have a fate of death, while only one will rule. Knowing this makes you want to resist connecting with the characters too much. Unfortunately, I found something I enjoyed about each of the sisters. I may have changed who I’m rooting for several times and even now am not sure who my actual favorite is. But if the plot rings true, only one can live.<br /><br />The book is written in third-person with each of the sister’s perspectives in addition to several other characters’ POV (some we see way less often than others). There are a variety characters including the families that raised the girls, friends, priestesses, and a couple love interests. It’s interesting how each sister is raised in a different city by a completely different family working on an entirely different gift. Each of these girls lives in a fully fleshed-out, complex world with their own characters and storylines. Though it’s all intertwined together, it still helps to make a plot that really moves along. There are plenty of twists and surprises throughout, a small bit of romance that doesn’t overwhelm, an epic world created, and the perfect amount of darkness. The ending had me screaming YES give me more!! I highly, highly recommend!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4544849629507547507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11905964781452104441" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450039832ra/17370784.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>this book was a real fcking treat. but i can't say i'm all that surprised given the description &amp; how much i love <br><br><b>~dark shit™~</b><br><br>so imma break it down for you like this: we got 3 black haired hoes (shhh i know, thats misogynistic of me whatever i do my part in dismantling the patriarchy too) and they got some POWERS<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483822606ra/21653460.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>more specifically we've got<br><br><b>kat the rat: </b><br>- overall pretty lame<br>- kind of described as a drowned rat, hence the name<br>- terrible taste in men<br><br><b>mirror mirror:</b><br>- also pretty lame but like she's kind of nice<br>- doesn't like slaughtering people even though it's kind of her job? get over urself, sis<br>- terrible taste in men, seriously what were you thinking<br><br><b>arsenic: </b><br>- the least lame<br>- wears pants (appreciate her trying to keep it spicy when she's forced to wear black everyday)<br>- pretty decent taste in men... but sweetie his name is billy so maybe not<br><br>annnnnd there's also a whole host of other insane ass side characters that i'm much too lazy to describe to you but rest assured they have equally as titillating character traits.<br><br><b>what do these hoes do you may ask</b><br><br>they try and kill each other! or like not yet, but that's kind of the point of the series. <s>one ring to rule them</s> one hoe wins the crown and the others go bye bye.<br><br><b>in all seriousness, i thought this was pretty excellent and i really appreciated the thought and detail that not only went into the world but also into the development of relationships. that's what makes books stand out to me. the three queens had distinct traits and their interactions with their own inner circles and with each other made them feel very real to me. and i mean cmon, the description alone for these is intriguing. i would highly recommend these to anyone who likes things with a historical fiction feel. maybe don't pick it up if you don't like political drama or slow moving plot. i wholeheartedly enjoyed this &amp; hopefully you enjoy these hoes too</b><br><br><i>also this was a buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/45365270-nadhira-satria" rel="nofollow noopener">nadhira</a> who is lovely and delightful and put up with me being slow as shit in the beginning and then finishing this book before her. she's a queen &amp; is a general treat to talk books with </i></span>

<div id="review_2021443898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021443898" />
    <a title="sreeja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja"><img alt="sreeja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598363186p2/50309540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021443898?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sreeja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sreeja" href="/user/show/50309540-sreeja">sreeja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50309540-sreeja?shelf=fantasy-reads">fantasy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50309540-sreeja?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021443898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6216725429692489571"><i>
  <b><br/>Three dark sisters<br/>All fair to be seen,<br/>Two to devour<br/>And one to be Queen”</b>
</i><br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/bcBx' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497367283ra/23016197.gif' alt='giphy0b1d9.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>well that was misleading and disappointing</b> <br/><br/>IDK if i should give this 1/2 stars?<br/><br/><b>LOOK I’M SORRY I REALLY WANTED TO LOVE THIS, I REALLY DID</b> (but it was really bad) <br/>I am so surprised I didn’t like this book because this kind of books are my kind of books. <i>I am so pissed</i> and disappointed. The ending part was a HUGE improvement but honestly not enough for me to actually like this.<br/><br/>OKAY but I’m a positive person so let me jus</span>
  <span id="freeText6216725429692489571" style="display:none"><i>
  <b><br>Three dark sisters<br>All fair to be seen,<br>Two to devour<br>And one to be Queen”</b>
</i><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bcBx" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497367283ra/23016197.gif" alt="giphy0b1d9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>well that was misleading and disappointing</b> <br><br>IDK if i should give this 1/2 stars?<br><br><b>LOOK I’M SORRY I REALLY WANTED TO LOVE THIS, I REALLY DID</b> (but it was really bad) <br>I am so surprised I didn’t like this book because this kind of books are my kind of books. <i>I am so pissed</i> and disappointed. The ending part was a HUGE improvement but honestly not enough for me to actually like this.<br><br>OKAY but I’m a positive person so let me just try and talk about the positive side of this book<br>The whole political aspect that this book had was probably one of the only interesting plot points in this book but even that didn’t feel well carried out. It was definitely very interesting to see the power struggles between the different factions of the island but boy was this book tedious. <br>I loved Katherine and Arsinoe, Mirabella was kind of just there to add drama. TBH I can’t even be bothered to think of the things that I actually liked about them. <br>OK LET ME SEE<br>um Katharine's character was really sweet and all and i felt with that ending we can see a more badass side of her and i am excited <br> <br>I probably loved Arsinoe the most she was very carefree and just badass but her chapters were <b>wasted on the love triangle</b> :) <br><br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/youre-invited-to-suffer-join-2468000_zpsl6rkmuxk.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488894416i/22165120.png" alt=" photo youre-invited-to-suffer-join-2468000_zpsl6rkmuxk.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Basically this book was a headache</i>&amp; I’m sorry I can’t even think about good stuff that happened.<br><br><b>okay unmarked spoilers from here on, because I’m just really done with this book and I’m not even going to bother, SO IF YOU WANT TO READ THIS BOOK, just don’t read from here on</b><br><br>This book was supposed to be dark and mysterious <i>so when did it turn into an angsty teen drama </i> with insta-love and love triangles. NO I did not sign up for this.<b>I HATE</b> the whole Joseph drama that we have going on in this book so much I can’t even begin to explain it. <br>First off, I hate Joseph Sandrin he is the definition of a fuckboy and i hate him. Like he is the main reason for this whole angsty teen drama to start in this book and I don’t understand his purpose in this book. He’s just this naturalist who is “so beautiful it hurts my eyes”.<br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bcBM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497367283ra/23016198.gif" alt="source640a0.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I love Arsinoe okay she seemed like a really great character and she had a ton of potential and I don’t understand why the author felt the need to use her chapters to explore Jules and Joseph’s relationship. <b>LIKE I don’t care about them.</b> Jules pretty much became a main character and like she’s a strong character and all but please don’t waste the precious Arsinoe chapters talking about how much they loved each other as kids. <br>I wouldn’t have mind Jules getting a huge chunk of the chapters if the author was idk explaining her powers or showing her being badass with her cougar (idek mountain cat?). I don’t want to see her moping around about Joesph all right?<b>LET ME JUST SAY,</b> this whole drama is the worst. So basically, Joseph decides to hop on his boat and go somewhere.<br><br> Meanwhile Mirabella; the precious princess runs away from her mansion because she needs to clear her head after having a bad dream. So she runs away and<i> decides to create a super devastating storm just because she feels like it and thought that it would be cool</i>. And our boy Joseph gets caught in this storm and nearly dies from drowning so Mirabella saves him, from the mess that she had created in the first place might I add. So he’s cold and lonely and “delirious” as he likes to say it and he decides to sleep with Mirabella after knowing her for 5 minutes. <i>WOW, what a great and totally necessary plot point we have here</i>. And all this while, Joseph pretty much gave a ring to Jules and is <b>“undyingly in love with her”</b>. Great way to show it Joseph, by sleeping with your best friend’s sister while you’re engaged to another girl. And Mirabella obviously gets dragged home and she is heartbroken because she fell in love with someone she met for 5 minutes. <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bcBW" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497367283i/23016199.jpg" alt="1800.jpgw300q55autoformatusm12fitmaxs356b2fb8057496771f377315626ded42d1eee.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Honestly, Mira should have just let Joseph drown and saved us from the love triangle and insta love. Also Elizabeth, Mira’s “best friend” gets her arm chopped off because she helped Mira run away just so that she could “clear her head” and also sleep with a stranger. And Elizabeth is chill with it. <i>In what world is a person</i> alright with their right arm being severed from their body for a human trashbag such as Mira. Honestly if I was Elizabeth I would set my pet loose on Mira and probably get Katharine to poison her to be on the safe side. <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bcBg" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1497367283i/23016200._SY540_.jpg" alt="The_Real_Story_Behind_Black_Guy_On_The_Phone_Meme-500x500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>BRB CALLING YOUR MOM MIRA.</b><br>What was the point of all this drama though? Can they all just become friends and I don’t know go all <i>John Tucker Must Die on Joseph</i>. Like stop hating each other please, pretty please?? Plus Mirabella and Jules would make good friends I don’t understand why their characters have to be stuck in a love triangle and hate each other. <br>Look this is not even the worst part of the book. This had so much potential to become an amazing story that was dark and gripping but nah. The world building was pretty much <i>non-existent</i> and that is what bothers me the most about this book, there is nearly 400 pages in this and still I did not come out of this book knowing anything about this world. I’m totally fine with fantasy books being slow but this book was slow without a purpose. Usually when a fantasy book is slow, the author is slowly building the world but nope that didn’t happen. <br> <b>This was probably the biggest disappointment.</b>The fact that it focuses more on love triangles and the sisters falling in love and long dramatic longing stares rather than having a gripping plot. I mean this could have been about badass sisters who yes, try to actually kill each other and it could have had amazing elements of strong female friendships and sisterhood. <b>BUT HA</b> it didn’t. Jules was such a great character and instead of being with her friend who could most probably die within the year she decides that it is for the best that she spends more time pining about her cheating boyfriend. Like no??? I want strong friendships and a dark/ gripping plot and this had none of it.<i> I feel cheated omg. </i><br>All the character’s plot points were just terrible. Katherine on one hand gets lessons from this guy Pietyr so she can make all the suitors fall in love with her during their meeting but what is the point??? If you and your sisters are going to start killing each other after the whole ceremony thing what is the point of Katherine learning how to seduce guys except for the cliché <i>“omg I don’t want any other guy I want you Pietyr”</i> plot line. It’s cute but really cliché. <br>Arsinoe had the whole low magic thing going on and <b>I WAS ACTUALLY INTERESTED</b>. But was that the main point of her chapters? No. It was the drama between Jules and Joesph. Spare me.<br>This being said the last 50-80 pages of this book was wayyy better than the rest but it didn’t feel worth it to drag myself through the few hundred pages to only have it be amazing in the last few chapters. The very ending though like w0t is every guy in this book going to be an asshole?? (except for Billy of course ily billy) That last line was a good last line though it was kind of surprising but not <br>Like that whole plot twist was interesting but I wasn’t even <i>THAT shocked</i>. For all the hype about how great that ending was IDK it didn’t feel like it blew me away you know?? <b>SO yeah</b> I was just there acting all fake surprised when all that shit went down in the last few chapters because I couldn’t really care about the characters.<br><a href="http://s1064.photobucket.com/user/simplysreeja/media/06b9ffe7-8230-41ed-b12d-3014108d1709_zpsqr00roxr.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490974768i/22365357.png" alt=" photo 06b9ffe7-8230-41ed-b12d-3014108d1709_zpsqr00roxr.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>There is like a huge hole</b> in my heart right now because what was this book? I actually feel really bad for not liking it&amp; this is the perfect example of why I am scared of hyped books. Okay but hopefully the next book will actually <i>focus more on magic and powers and people trying to kill each other</i> rather than the sisters being caught up in drama and love triangles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6216725429692489571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1762666669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1762666669" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1577828317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577828317" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1577828317?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23207027-three-dark-crowns">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=lost-the-will-to-live">lost-the-will-to-live</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=love-stinks">love-stinks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=never-call-me-again">never-call-me-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1577828317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4527690515175643691">How could a book with such a promising premise fall so flat? (This is a stupid question and by now, having been a Goodreads member for seven years, I ought to know better.)<br/><br/>The thing is, right, that the first chapter was absolutely mesmerizing. In fact, Katharine remained the only character I was even mildly interested in for the rest of the book. But sometimes I like to look at it this way: if I were a literary agent, and this book came into my query inbox, and the author had attached the first </span>
  <span id="freeText4527690515175643691" style="display:none">How could a book with such a promising premise fall so flat? (This is a stupid question and by now, having been a Goodreads member for seven years, I ought to know better.)<br /><br />The thing is, right, that the first chapter was absolutely mesmerizing. In fact, Katharine remained the only character I was even mildly interested in for the rest of the book. But sometimes I like to look at it this way: if I were a literary agent, and this book came into my query inbox, and the author had attached the first five pages, then I would have requested the full manuscript. That's how good the first chapter was. <br /><br />Everything after the first chapter was punishing. Absolutely nothing about Arsinoe, or the limp, anticlimactic backstory of Jules and Joseph, is in any way interesting. Mirabella is just another special girl who can control the elements, the same as the 95,000 other YA heroines who can "command fire" or "command water". Elemental power is so fucking tired at this point, while I know that any overused trope can be reinvented to be fresh, this book doesn't manage it. It's dry as fuck.<br /><br />Whatever, dude. I'm bored of even writing this review. I'm bored just thinking about this book. But the thing is, right, I was promised a story about a deathly showdown between three sisters (remarkably relatable for me) and what I got was bland shite romance and nonsensical world building and overused tropes that feel overused. Just a giant meh from me, I think. <br /><br />FIN</span>
  <a data-text-id="4527690515175643691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1763566498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1639025202303672605">3.25/5. but a FUN 3.25!!<br/><br/>This book was far from perfect, but hell if it wasn’t a good time. And after two not so fun reads, I needed it!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477350526ra/20941172.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2016/10/26/three-dark-crowns-review/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>Did I like any of the characters? Uh, not totally. In fact, I hated a bunch of them. (I would physically fight Mirabella and Joseph if I was ever given the chance, and I would like roughly 50% of the characters to line up so I can efficiently slap each of them across the face.) Most of them were super flat--I’d say all of t</span>
  <span id="freeText1639025202303672605" style="display:none">3.25/5. but a FUN 3.25!!<br><br>This book was far from perfect, but hell if it wasn’t a good time. And after two not so fun reads, I needed it!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477350526ra/20941172.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2016/10/26/three-dark-crowns-review/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br><br>Did I like any of the characters? Uh, not totally. In fact, I hated a bunch of them. (I would physically fight Mirabella and Joseph if I was ever given the chance, and I would like roughly 50% of the characters to line up so I can efficiently slap each of them across the face.) Most of them were super flat--I’d say all of them except Arsinoe, Jules and maybe Pietyr. (That’s pretty insane because there are roughly 200 characters in this book.)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474436474ra/20597856.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The three queens are not my ideal. I was hoping for a little more badassery in all honesty. Mirabella is an emotional idiot (who became best friends with some rando in a day, which reminded me SO MUCH of my Justin Bieber fanfiction-reading days. Except instead of like, Selena Gomez or Demi Lovato, Mira’s bestie is a shockingly flat priestess). Katharine starts out the same way, and Arsinoe is just kind of...eh. Maybe they'll bond in the next book over their mutual terribleness.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477350526ra/20941173.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The world building was a little rough, too. This is one of those books that’ll give you a furrowed brow for the first chunk. The whole thing was surprisingly low fantasy for how confusing it was. Props to Blake for not info-dumping, but the weaving in of background was a little slow for my tastes. Also, there are like a bajillion names in this? The map is, though pretty, very confusing, and the time I spent figuring out who Ellis was gave me a headache. And maybe I’m a nerd, but I also just want a history lesson on this world. That’s such a fun part of fantasy books!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477350526i/20941174.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though this book had a LOT of problems (and didn’t really make it to a lot of the fun stuff they spent the whole time talking about?) it was still pretty fun. So I don’t want to give it a low rating. <br><br>I’d be giving this book 3 stars if not for the literal last sentence. It filled me with hope for more bad bitches, gave me a halfhearted belief that maybe (MAYBE) I’ll actually like a certain character next time around, and made me wanna pick up the next book. So it’s not over, folks.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458165623ra/18452129.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bottom line: yeah, read this! It’s just a little silly and a little fun, and I’m looking forward to the rest of the books.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2151078767833660849">Rating: 2.5 stars<br/><br/>I've been wanting to read this for the longest time because the synopsis sounded so good. Maybe the anticipation contributed a bit, maybe it didn't, but this fell flat for me. <br/><br/>I was expecting a fast-paced, action-driven story with a lot of intrigue and strategy, but I was forcing myself to push through, even when the pace improved.   <span id="freeText2151078767833660849" style="display:none">Rating: 2.5 stars<br /><br />I've been wanting to read this for the longest time because the synopsis sounded so good. Maybe the anticipation contributed a bit, maybe it didn't, but this fell flat for me. <br /><br />I was expecting a fast-paced, action-driven story with a lot of intrigue and strategy, but I was forcing myself to push through, even when the pace improved. Most of the characters, including the 3 young queens, were flat and I often had trouble understanding their motivations. I wanted more development and an insight into their desires, but without these their actions weren't always believable.<br /><br />I was pretty confident that I wasn't going to continue the series until I hit the last page... I'll admit I'm now curious to know what will happen next, but I'm not sure if it's enough to actually pick up the sequel. Do the later books improve?</span>

<div id="review_1682811434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1682811434" />
    <a title="Ben Alderson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15850647-ben-alderson"><img alt="Ben Alderson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485420738p2/15850647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1682811434?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ben Alderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ben Alderson" href="/user/show/15850647-ben-alderson">Ben Alderson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
